International Labor Conference to Be Held Again 117

Selection of Representatives

The 15th International Labor Conference will be held in Geneva, Switzerland, on May 28th of this year. China only started participating after the establishment of the National Government. The employer representative is nominated by the National Federation of Chambers of Commerce from among domestic industrialists. Last year, Wu Qintai was invited to attend the 14th conference as the employer representative, with Sun Zunxian as his advisor. The government sent Ma Chaojun as its representative. The 15th conference is about to be held, and a reporter from the Guowen News Agency visited the National Federation of Chambers of Commerce to inquire about the matter. The relevant documents are compiled as follows:

Order from the Ministry of Industry: Regarding the matter of compliance, the 15th International Labor Conference is scheduled to be held in Geneva, Switzerland, on May 28th of this year. The Ministry has drafted a proposal on the method of sending representatives and advisors to attend this conference and submitted it to the 14th State Council Meeting of the Executive Yuan for discussion. It was decided to send it to the Central Political Conference. Now, the Executive Yuan Order No. 1205 opens with: "Regarding the handling of the matter, the letter from the Civil Service Office of the National Government No. 1903 opens with: 'Regarding the matter of the letter from the Central Political Conference approving the Executive Yuan's letter transmitting Minister Kong Xiangxi's proposal to formulate measures and budget for sending representatives to the 15th International Labor Conference for review, etc., the 264th meeting of this conference resolved to pass the measures and the budget to the Finance Group for review. In addition to sending the budget after the decision, the case is recorded and the original proposal is enclosed for reference and handling.' In accordance with the Chairman's instructions to the Executive Yuan, etc., in addition to replying to the letter, a copy of the original document is sent for your reference." According to this, the measures in the resolution regarding the dispatch of employer representatives and advisors should be jointly proposed by the China Industrial Association Federation and the National Federation of Chambers of Commerce of the Republic of China and submitted to the government for approval. As the conference is approaching, the candidates for these representatives and advisors must be determined urgently. In addition to the separate orders, the Ministry encloses its proposal and orders the association to jointly determine the candidates with the China Industrial Association Federation and report them to the Ministry for submission to the government for approval.

Minister Kong's Proposal: The measures proposed by Minister Kong at the State Council meeting are as follows: Regarding the proposal, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs sent a letter from the International Labor Office regarding the notice of the 15th International Labor Conference, requesting review, etc. After checking the Ministry, the meeting is scheduled to be held in Geneva, Switzerland, on May 28th of this year. The seven issues to be discussed are mostly important, especially the election of the members of the Board of Directors, which is a key three-year re-election. China has expressed its hope to obtain a seat on the Board of Directors in previous conferences. At this time, it is necessary to strive for election in order to achieve the initial goal. As the opening date is approaching, the measures for sending representatives should be prepared in advance to facilitate the process. The measures for sending representatives are as follows: (1) Sending Representatives: (A) Government representatives are proposed to be nominated by the Ministry as in the past and submitted for approval. The first representative will be selected and sent from the country, and the other will be selected from among the foreign envoys. (B) Employer representatives were previously nominated by the National Federation of Chambers of Commerce. This year, the China Industrial Association Federation has been established. The proposals of this conference are related to both industry and commerce. Regarding the selection of employer representatives, it is proposed that the two associations jointly nominate one representative and submit it to the government for approval. (C) Labor representatives are proposed to be nominated by the Central Party Headquarters in consultation with the labor community and submitted by the government for approval as in previous years. (2) Selection of Advisors and Secretaries: (A) Government advisors and secretaries. The proposals of this conference are mostly important, and experts should be selected for consultation. Regarding the discussion of the age of children in non-industrial work and the revision of the Convention on Night Work for Women, in accordance with the letter from the International Labor Office and the provisions of the Treaty of Versailles, one woman must be selected as an advisor. This time, it is proposed to send three advisors (one of whom is a woman) and one secretary, who will be selected by the Ministry from those who are familiar with international labor affairs, and submitted for approval. (B) Employer advisors are proposed to be jointly nominated by the China Industrial Association Federation and the National Federation of Chambers of Commerce and submitted to the government. (C) Labor advisors are proposed to be nominated by the Central Party Headquarters and then submitted by the government for approval. (3) The government plans to send a total of people this time. The expenditure for the delegation is expected to be higher as one additional woman is assigned as an advisor than in the previous years. Furthermore, the price of gold has doubled this year compared to last year; the expense for attending this conference has to be increased accordingly. Regarding the issues to be discussed at this conference, the Ministry is currently formulating counter-proposals based on investigations and references to domestic conditions, and is studying competitive strategies for the election of members of the Board of Directors for the attending representatives to carry out. Is it appropriate to prepare the measures for sending representatives to the 15th International Labor Conference? Please review and decide the expenditure for the attending representatives.

Letter to the Industrial Federation: The National Federation of Chambers of Commerce sent a letter to the China Industrial Association Federation yesterday, stating: We are writing to inform you that we have received the Order No. 220 from the Ministry of Industry (omitted in the middle), etc. In accordance with this, we are writing to inform your association for verification. Please reply to us regarding how to handle this case.

Reactions to the Shanghai Municipal Council's Estimated Rent Collection 118

Statement from the Real Estate Association: Li Bohan, the standing committee member of the Real Estate Association, told a reporter from the Guowen News Agency yesterday that the collection of housing taxes in the Public Concession has always been calculated according to the actual rent and based on the house bill. This is a common principle in municipal administration in various countries. This time, the Shanghai Municipal Council organized a rent valuation committee and invited our association to nominate a Chinese representative to serve as a member of the committee. The legislative intent is to focus on the self-owned residences of property owners who do not have house bills to indicate the amount of rent. When there is a dispute between the taxation department and the property owner, the member will be responsible for arbitration. However, our association absolutely insists on the decades-long practice of basing the rent on the house bill and will not allow any changes. If the Shanghai Municipal Council calculates the rent based on estimated rent, the harms will be immeasurable. Because the estimated rent has no legal basis, the tenants will suffer from the pain of arbitrarily increasing the tax rate. The Shanghai Municipal Council will have unlimited ways to extract money, which will cause disputes and resentment in the future, and will run counter to the purpose of hoping for the prosperity of the municipal administration in the Concession. This kind of plan only seeks financial revenue and disregards the burden on the citizens, which is unfair and should be immediately cancelled. Our association will soon send a serious protest to the Shanghai Municipal Council, with the main text in Chinese and an English translation attached.

Public Letter from Zhongshe: Shanghai Zhongshe sent a letter to the Chinese Ratepayers Association of the Shanghai International Settlement yesterday, stating: We are writing to inform you that our company's houses are rented from Huazhong Company, with a lease agreement stating that the monthly rent is 350 taels from 144 Weihaiwei Road to 156, with the Huazhong lease and receipts as proof. The Shanghai Municipal Council should calculate the general municipal tax according to the actual amount of rent. Unexpectedly, they have estimated it to be 520 taels without authorization. Although our company submitted the lease agreement, rent receipts, and a certificate from Huazhong stating the reason for calculating our company's rent, requesting the Shanghai Municipal Council to correct it, they replied that they did not explain the reasons for the valuation and did not express any opinion on the evidence submitted by our company, only stating that the Shanghai Municipal Council has the right to estimate the price, and rejected our company's reasonable request without considering it. Our company's houses belong to the Jing'an Villa range leased by Huazhong. The city houses along Jing'an Temple Road each occupy ten squares of land, with a construction cost of over 1,000 taels per square and a land price of over 50,000 taels per acre. Our company occupies a total of 30 squares of land, with a construction cost of less than 900 taels per square and a land price of less than 30,000 taels per acre, because the original plan was to build a garage, which was later changed to a club by our company's agreement with Huazhong Company. The buildings are far inferior to the city houses along Jing'an Temple Road in Jing'an Villa, but the rent of the city houses is only 130 taels per house, which is better than our company's monthly rent of 350 taels in terms of the ratio of investment benefits. Calculating the general municipal tax at 350 taels is not incorrect (omitted in the middle). We are especially sending the drafts of the letters we have sent to the Shanghai Municipal Council and various evidence to your association for your assistance in fighting for our rights. In addition to sending a separate letter to the Shanghai Municipal Council stating that we have applied to your association for negotiation, we will send the general municipal tax of 14% of the actual rent of 350 taels, totaling 147 taels, directly to the Shanghai Municipal Council. If the Shanghai Municipal Council refuses to accept it, the responsibility for the delay should be borne by the Shanghai Municipal Council. Please state this together.

Weng Tonglu, Destitute and Homeless, Commits Suicide by Poisoning in a Hotel 126

A Suicide Note to Three Cousins

"Family Members Need Not Grieve"

Weng Tonglu, a 28-year-old man from Ningbo, was formerly in the foreign goods business. Recently, due to unemployment, he had been idle for a long time, drifting in Shanghai with nothing to do. His parents, wife, and children were all in his hometown. Now, due to the economic pressure he felt, he suddenly became suicidal. On the evening of the 28th, at 8:00 PM, he went to the Siming Hotel (newly opened) at No. 96, next to Yuqing Lane, at the intersection of Xizilaihuo Street and Damalu in the French Concession. He checked in under the changed name of Shi Erqing into a small room on the third floor, No. 38, and paid one yuan for the room. After the waiter brought in tea, Weng closed the door and wrote a suicide note. After writing it, he swallowed poison and committed suicide. After taking the poison, he went to sleep. The next day at noon, the waiter, Dong Awu, saw that Weng had not yet gotten up, and the time had passed the hotel's regulations, so he knocked on the door to ask if the room was needed. Weng replied, "I'll sleep a little longer." At 3:00 PM, he knocked on the door again, but there was no response. Knowing that something was wrong, he informed the accountant and notified someone from the Hotel Industry Association to come and force open the door. They found that Weng had died. His body was still warm. They found a suicide note and reported it to the police station, which sent detectives to investigate. They took the body to the Tongren Fuyuan Branch Hall for an autopsy. The suicide note was addressed to his cousins, Weng Tongkang, Tongzi, and Tongchuan. He recounted the economic pressure and difficulties in life that led to his suicide. He asked them to take care of the aftermath and comfort his parents and wife, telling them not to grieve. Finally, he instructed them to cremate his body. The address on the letter was No. 59, Shuangguili, Kangti Road, Father Du Road. The detectives went to the address and found Weng Tongkang, a relative of the deceased, who identified the body. Yesterday, the Criminal Section of the French Police Station reported to the French Court. The judge, upon inspecting the scene, confirmed that the deceased had committed suicide by taking poison and ordered photographs to be taken. He approved Weng Tongkang's request to prepare a coffin and collect the body. Tongkang has now urged the deceased's parents and wife to come to Shanghai to collect the body.

New Sewage Disposal Plant Being Built in the Public Garden 127

Does Not Affect the Scenery of the Park

The North China Daily News reports that the extraordinary development of the central district of the Public Concession in recent years has rendered the sewage disposal plant built on the Bund of Beijing Road ten years ago inadequate, necessitating the construction of a new plant. The construction work currently underway inside the fence in the Bund Public Garden is the building of this new plant. According to the report, the original plant on the Bund of Beijing Road was equipped with two pumping stations that transported sewage collected from the ditches east of Henan Road across the Waibaidu Bridge to the sewage plant in the eastern district. The new plant being built in the park will be equipped with the latest inventions. Two larger pumping stations will be temporarily installed, and another pumping station may be added in the future. The pumping station is 20 feet deep and entirely underground. Once completed, the exterior will be no different and will not affect the scenery of the park. The underground room of the original plant on the Bund of Beijing Road will be demolished and the pumping station will be replaced with a steel curtain to separate hard materials in the pipes.

Mental Breakdown Leads to Suicide by Jumping from Building 129

Wang Afu, a 40-year-old man from Anhui, had been renting a room at the Mingli Inn (a small hotel) on Guizhi Road in Wusong for a long time. He had no occupation and suffered from occasional mental illness. The day before yesterday, after dinner, Wang left the Mingli Inn. Later, he went to the home of his friend, a Mr. Wu, at No. 15 Nanchang Road. Wu invited him to chat on the bed upstairs. At that time, his expression showed no strangeness. At about 10:00 PM, Wang and his friend were chatting and laughing happily on the bed when someone knocked on the door downstairs urgently. Wu was about to go downstairs to open the door when Wang, hearing the knocking, seemed startled and suddenly had a relapse of his mental illness. His attitude changed drastically, and he jumped from the bed and out of the window. Wu was shocked to see this and rushed to save him, but it was too late. He fell from the window and landed in the courtyard on a water tank. His friend immediately went downstairs to inspect and saw that the water tank was broken and Wang was lying in a pool of blood with his head resting on the broken tank, severely injured and barely breathing. His friend and neighbors immediately carried the injured man to the Seashore Public Hospital on Wai Malu. The hospital refused to accept him because his internal organs were damaged and it was difficult to treat him. The injured man was carried back to the Mingli Inn and died there yesterday morning. Afterwards, because Wang had no family members in Song, his body was purchased with donations from his friend and the owner of the Mingli Inn. A coffin was purchased, and he was buried at the Zhenbei Cemetery in the afternoon. They are trying to find Wang's family members to come to Song to claim the body.

Zhang Tiankai Acquitted of Gun Charge 130

Zhang Tiankai, owner of the Tiankai Xiang Bulb Factory on Edouard Avenue and a native of Fengjing, was deceived by the slander of his accountant, Chang Huinan, and severely reprimanded Ma Haiwen, a Xiang native who was the doorkeeper, for not driving away passers-by who urinated in the lane next to the factory. Ma did not admit his negligence and responded with harsh words, which angered Zhang, who opened fire and fired two shots that missed. Ma sued him to the police station and was taken to the Special District Local Court, which prosecuted him for obstructing freedom. The official ordered the defendant to pay 5,000 yuan as bail pending trial. The details have been reported previously. Yesterday morning, witnesses Cai Heshang, Zhang Dabao, Shen Yushu, Li Xingfa, etc. were summoned to testify and said that Ma Wenhai had actually started the fight by hitting Chang Huinan first. When Zhang arrived at the factory, Ma grabbed an iron bar and rushed towards Zhang, uttering abusive words and threatening to beat him. Zhang then held a pistol and ordered him to throw away the iron bar. Because Ma did not listen, Zhang fired two shots at the ground. The defendant continued to be defended by lawyers Jiang Yiping and Zheng Wenkai, who argued that the defendant fired the gun purely in self-defense. After the debate with the police lawyer ended, Judge Ge carefully examined the case and declared that the police's prosecution of the case under Article 319 of the Criminal Law for obstructing freedom was inappropriate. Therefore, the case could not be established and Zhang Tiankai was immediately declared not guilty. He was still required to pay the original bail during the appeal period.

Laborer Crushed to Death by Car 131

Yesterday at about 3:15 PM, a heavy vehicle was passing over the Lihong Bridge in Hongkou. When the vehicle went off the bridge, its momentum was very strong. Unfortunately, the laborer pulling the rope in front of the vehicle slipped on the mud and fell, causing the wheel to crush his abdomen and injure vital parts. He died on the spot. Several companions, seeing the cause of the disaster, feared being implicated and quickly pulled the car away without a trace. Street guards No. 1549 saw this and chased after the driver of the car that caused the accident, but were unsuccessful. They could only send the body to the Tongren Hospital and then to the Coroner's office for an autopsy. The deceased was wearing a short black cloth shirt, blue cloth trousers, had a shaved head, and was barefoot. He was approximately 30 years old.

Automobile Accident Injures Jiang Caisheng 132

Cai Zhenting Submitted to the Public Security Bureau

Jiang Caisheng, an employee of the Dahua Socks Factory, was walking outside Xiaobeimen around 4 p.m. the other day when he was suddenly knocked down from behind by a passing car, injuring his face, nose, and upper and lower front teeth. The injury was quite serious. At the time, the car sped away. The police officer on duty was unable to catch up, only vaguely remembering the car's concession license number as 9226. He then took the injured person to the First Precinct of the Second District. After investigation, Xu, the station chief, determined that Jiang Caisheng's injury was severe and ordered him to seek treatment at a hospital. However, Jiang Caisheng was poor and had no funds, so he went to Renji Hospital. The doctor found that his injury was quite serious and had not yet healed. The First Precinct of the Second District sent a letter to the Public Works Bureau to investigate. It was found that the car involved in the accident belonged to the Yinghai Automobile Company in Xiaonanmen. The driver, Cai Zhenting, was summoned for questioning as to why he sped away after causing the accident. Cai denied the charge. The officer on duty provided evidence, and it was determined that the driver, Cai Zhenting, should be submitted to the Public Security Bureau for severe punishment to serve as a warning for the future.

Unidentified Male Corpse Found South of Xinlonghua 133

A nameless male corpse, estimated to be around 60 years old, was discovered on the 24th of this month in the riverbank east of the Shi family residence, south of Xinlonghua in West Shanghai. The local bailiff, Pan Caisheng, reported it to the court. The court appointed Prosecutor Wu Deying to go to the countryside with a coroner to inspect the corpse. The inspection revealed that the corpse had drowned itself before death. The coroner ordered that photos be taken and the corpse be handed over to the local bailiff to prepare a coffin, collect the body, and temporarily place it in a temple to await identification. Unexpectedly, a man went to the Third Precinct of the Sixth District of the Municipal Public Security Bureau the day before yesterday, claiming that his name was Wei Guanquan, 41 years old, from Shenzhuang Town, Nanhui County. His father, named A Xu, 61 years old, took 46 silver dollars on the first train to Changqiao Town on the 21st of this month to buy a cow. Before leaving, he said that he would return in three days. Until the 16th, he had not returned home. The family was extremely anxious. He had no choice but to go out to search. He went to Xia Yusheng's house in Xiajia Village, Changqiao Town, to inquire. According to Xia Yusheng, his father had come once near evening on the 21st and again on the morning of the 23rd. Later, because there was no cow to buy, he went back. According to Xia Abing's mother, his father came a second time (i.e., on the 23rd) and went to the town with Xia Yusheng to smoke, etc. He asked Xia Yusheng where his father went after smoking with him. Xia firmly claimed that he did not know and did not go to town to smoke with him. He then went to Gujia Village's dairy shed to inquire about his father's whereabouts and whether Xia Yusheng had been there. According to a village woman, a few days ago, Xia Yusheng and an unfamiliar old man did come to Gu Xiaolong's house to buy a cow, but they did not succeed. In the evening, they went back together. He was extremely anxious. Later, he heard that an unidentified male corpse was found in the riverbank east of the Shi family residence north of Changqiao Town on the 24th of this month. According to villagers, the age and appearance of the corpse were similar to his father. He immediately went to the court to investigate and saw a photo of the corpse. It was indeed his father. However, according to the coroner, there were no injuries, and there were only dozens of copper coins on his body, nothing else. The silver dollars he had brought and the black cotton robe and gray long shirt he had on were all missing. The cause of his father's death was unknown. Xia Yusheng was highly suspected. He pleaded to detain him and seek justice for him, weeping uncontrollably as he spoke. After receiving the report, Chief Liu immediately dispatched a senior police officer to arrest Xia Yusheng overnight. Xia confessed that he was 43 years old and lived in Xiajia Village, Changqiao Town. He admitted that he went to buy a cow with the deceased, but he did not know how he died. Chief Liu considered the case to be a serious one involving murder for money and immediately prepared a document yesterday afternoon, sending the corpse, the son of the deceased Wei Guanquan, and the suspect Xia Yusheng to the bureau to await investigation and verification.

Moving of a Corpse on Zhongxing Road 134

Head and Shoulders Injured by Wooden Object

A wounded unidentified male corpse, about 30 years old, was discovered in the alley entrance at 115 Zhongxing Road, Zhabei yesterday morning. The inspection revealed that the corpse's head and left and right shoulders were injured by a wooden object, resulting in death. It was determined to be a case of corpse moving. The body was ordered to be collected by a charity organization to await investigation of the family and apprehension of the murderer.

Opium Hidden in Wooden Stool 138

At around 6 a.m. yesterday morning, at the Shanghai South Railway Station of the Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway, the station was preparing to depart the second early express train to Hangzhou. A passenger carrying a wooden stool arrived at the station to buy a ticket. The passenger lingered near the ticket window and looked suspicious. Tan Xianchao and Chen Jiaqi, the station police, stepped forward to question him. The passenger was evasive in his answers. They took the passenger and the wooden stool to the station master's office together. Station Master Zhou opened the stool and found miscellaneous items in the drawer, but the stool was inlaid with thin boards all around and weighed more than usual. He pried open the wooden boards and found a large amount of opium in the compartment. The opium was taken out and weighed, totaling 84 taels. The police took the person and the contraband to the South Station Police Department for questioning. The person confessed that his name was Zhao Honglu from Taizhou. Today, he met an unfamiliar man on Daxin Street, Simailu, who gave him this wooden stool and asked him to carry it to the South Station to take the train for two jiao. The man did not come with him. He did not know that there was opium stored in the stool. Chief Zhuang of the police department believed that the suspect was not telling the truth and was extremely cunning and an old drug dealer. He immediately prepared a document and sent the police to escort the suspect to the court for interrogation.

Dr. Huang Zhongqiang Opens a Medical Practice 143

Local News 2

Qu Songjia's Safe Escape After Being Kidnapped 144

Five Male and Female Kidnappers Have Been Arrested

Qu Songjia Will Go to Another Port to Recuperate

The Mastermind is Gu Huichang

The Security Team Supplied the Guns

The Kidnapping Cost 1,000 Yuan

Secret Meetings Held in the Park Each Time

Qu Songjia, the manager of the China Bank branch outside Xiaodongmen in the Nanshi district of this city, was kidnapped by bandits at around 8 a.m. on the 16th of this month when he was taking his private chartered car to the bank to work. At the time, due to the request of his family, the newspapers did not disclose the information. It is now heard that Mr. Qu has escaped and returned home yesterday. The details of the entire incident are supplemented below.

Branch Manager Rides in Chartered Car Mr. Qu is 34 years old, a local resident, and the second son of Qu Changshun, who runs a fish shop in Xiaodongmen. He is currently the manager of the Nanshi China Bank branch. His home is located at No. 3 Shenghao Lane, Dong Yaojia Lane, under the jurisdiction of the Second Precinct of the First District in Nanshi. Mr. Qu is young and strong, but he is quite frugal and only has one chartered car for transportation. On the 16th of this month, Mr. Qu got up in the morning, washed, and finished his meal. He took the chartered car to go to the bank to work. The driver, Jiang Hongqing (from Tongzhou, 33 years old, introduced by Tang Afu, a driver from the Ding family in Qiaojiabang, on the ninth day of the ninth lunar month last year), had just dropped off Qu's son at school and returned home. The car was parked at the entrance of the lane, waiting for the master's order.

Interference with Urination Leads to Kidnapping At 8:15 a.m., Qu came downstairs and got into the car. The driver was just pulling up the car's shaft, but before he could start, he saw a person wearing a dark-colored silk long gown walking into the lane, looking like he was going to urinate. Qu saw this and shouted that the place was not for urination. Unexpectedly, this person ran to the front of the car, first grabbing the driver's chest and twisting his clothes, then pulling out a pistol and shouting for the car to stop. At the same time, two people ran in from the entrance of the lane and dragged Qu out of the chartered car, telling him not to make a sound. The two men grabbed Qu's arms and pushed him out of the lane into a car that was parked on the side of the road, and sped away. The chartered car driver quickly returned home to inform Qu's older brother. They then went out to inspect the lane, but the people and the car had disappeared without a trace. Qu's family immediately reported the situation to the Second Precinct of the First District, requesting an arrest.

A Letter Suddenly Appears Earlier, the Dalu Automobile Company on Zhaopulu suddenly received a young man in a Western-style suit, about 20 years old, at 6:50 a.m. that morning. He rented a car to be sent to Fook Kai Sum Road in the French Concession, agreeing to a rental fee of $1.50. The young man took out two dollars, and the cashier gave him back 50 cents. He then ordered the driver, Zhuo Shiliang (from Ningbo, 32 years old), to drive car number 17688 in the concession, municipal number 511, to the destination. When the car arrived at the corner of Fook Kai Sum Road and Route Doumer, the young man ordered the driver to stop the car. He took out a letter from his pocket and ordered the driver to deliver it to a nearby dairy stand. The driver refused. While they were arguing, two people suddenly jumped out from the side of the road.

Borrowing a Car to Carry Out the Kidnapping After the two jumped out, each produced a pistol and forced the driver out of the car, forbidding him from making a sound. They then dragged him to a pine forest nearby and sat him on the ground. The young man in the Western-style suit drove the car away himself. The two men watched the driver for about an hour, then used hemp rope to tie the driver's hands and feet behind his back. The two then fled together. The driver struggled for a long time to remove the ropes and immediately ran to report to the detective head in the Route Tenant police station. The detective head immediately telephoned the Public Security Bureau and various police stations in the Public Concession to pay attention to intercepting the car. At the same time, the Second Precinct of the First District learned of this news and realized that the car used to kidnap Qu was rented by the bandits from the Dalu Automobile Company.

Mistakenly Reported Car Number When the French police dispatched telegrams to various police stations, they mistakenly reported the car number 511 as 571. After the Public Security Bureau's Supervisory Office received the report, it immediately sent Detective Captain Lu Ying and his team, including team leader Qi Haitain and detectives Zhou Peisan, Zhang Xinglong, and Han Ruisheng, to the Public Works Bureau to inspect the car registration books. They found that car number 571 belonged to the Ruan Ji Automobile Company at 581 Zhonghua Road, Dadongmen. They immediately went to the company and impounded car number 571. The company made various explanations. Captain Lu telegraphed the Second Precinct of the First District again and learned of the mistake. He then took car number 571 to the Dalu Automobile Company on Zhaopulu to inquire about the truth.

A False Alarm At that time, various police stations in the Public Concession also learned of the kidnapping case in the Chinese area. The reported car number was also mistakenly reported as municipal number 571. Therefore, additional Chinese and foreign detectives were stationed at various checkpoints to pay attention to interception. At that time, Captain Lu and others were driving car number 571 to the Baidu Bridge. The detectives there saw the car number arrive and saw five or six burly men sitting in the car. They believed it was the bandits' car. Everyone raised their guns and impounded the car. After repeated explanations, the misunderstanding was cleared up. However, the tense situation at the time caused the detectives to experience a false alarm.

Ransom Demanded 500,000 Yuan After Qu was kidnapped, his family received five letters from the bandits demanding a ransom of 500,000 yuan. Police Commissioner Chen of the Municipal Public Security Bureau immediately ordered his subordinates to solve the case within a limited time. As a result, detectives were dispatched from various districts. It was then discovered that a kidnapper named Peng Yaozhi (also known as Tang Mobang) was hiding in the 16th pier area. This was discovered by Xu Tao, a police officer from the Sixth District of the Municipal Public Security Bureau. He reported it to the First Precinct headquarters, which dispatched police officers and detectives, including team leader Dong Mingde and detectives Yuan Haishan, Yu Maolong, Lu Anpu, Ren Shouzheng, and Xu Yulin, to investigate for many days. They were able to arrest the bandit. During the preliminary interrogation, Peng confessed that he was 26 years old and from Qidong. He came to Shanghai from Zhenjiang in November of last year and lodged at the Nankang Inn in the 16th pier area. He was introduced to Gu Huichang by his friend Xiao Yuan.

Mastermind Gu Huichang Peng further confessed that Gu had persuaded him to join his gang to do a big deal. He claimed that the capital would be provided by someone and the guns would be supplied by Chen Xiaobing (also known as Lianchu, nicknamed Chen Dwarf), the head of the Chuansha Security Team, who lived near Qingning Temple in Pudong. He heard and declined the offer, but later introduced two friends to them to join the gang and do the deal. The original team of detectives were then ordered to go to Chuansha County in Pudong to arrest Chen Xiaobing. Chen did open a butcher shop and a water shop there, but he had already fled after hearing the news. He then returned to Shanghai and was arrested in the Gu Family Hall at the Hai Chao Temple in Xiaonanmen, along with the mastermind Gu Huichang and Gu's mistress, Ms. Shen.

Secret Meetings in the French Park After detectives from the First Precinct arrested the mastermind Gu Huichang (nicknamed Long Legs, 34 years old, a local resident) and his mistress, Ms. Shen (39 years old, a local resident), they interrogated them in detail. Gu confessed that he had colluded with Xiao Yang, Zhang Erlang, and three others to take three pistols and kidnap Qu. Initially, they hid him in Wei Family Flower Garden in Longhua for four days. On the fourth night, they used a small boat to send the hostage to the countryside of Chuansha. They stayed there for two days. Because the situation in Shanghai was urgent, they hid him at Tang Family Residence, about twelve miles southeast of Chuansha. The money for this kidnapping was provided by his cousin, Gu Zhong'an, totaling 1,000 yuan. The three pistols were supplied by Chen Xiaobing (also known as Chen Lianchu, nicknamed Dwarf), a member of the Chuansha Security Team. Secret meetings were held in the French Park each time.

Bandit's Mistress Reveals the Location After detectives received the confession, they immediately took Gu and more than ten police officers across the river overnight and ordered Gu to lead the way to make the arrest. However, Gu was cunning and kept dragging the detectives around all night, never revealing the true location of the hostage. The detectives were exhausted and returned. The second time, they went across the river with the suspect again, but found nothing. Finally, the bandit's mistress, Ms. Shen, revealed the location. Yesterday, they went directly to the Tang Family Residence to rescue the hostage. However, the hostage had been sent back to Shanghai by the bandits the night before last (the 28th). Only two women, Ms. Tang Zhang and Zhang Erlang, the hostage guard, were arrested. Zhang confessed that he was 65 years old and from Chuansha. He only remembered that a guest was sent by his son-in-law, Chen Lianchu (i.e., Xiaobing), on March 23 of the lunar calendar. The night before last (the 28th), Chen ordered her husband, Tang Zhirong, and two others to send the guest back to Shanghai. She did not know anything else.

Hostage Confirmed to Be Safe When asked, Zhang Erlang, 28 years old, from Chongming, confessed that he was guarding the hostage and did not deny it. He also claimed that when the hostage was hidden in the Tang Family Residence, he and the other guards were blindfolded and could not recognize each other's faces. As for the reason for sending the hostage back, he heard that it was because the situation was urgent and could not be delayed any longer. When asked where the hostage was, he confessed that he did not know. Detectives went to Qu's house to inquire. According to his family, Qu himself had called a moment ago, saying that he was safe and staying at a friend's house and would not be returning home for the time being. He would go to another port to recuperate in a few days. However, the family did not know where he was. The detectives saw that the family was unwilling to reveal the location, but since he was already safe, there was no need to investigate further. They returned to report to the district chief.

Strict Arrest of Accomplices at Large After District Chief Chen of the First District learned that the hostage was safe, he sent the detailed confessions of the 1,000 case criminals to the General Bureau for verification. At the same time, he ordered his subordinates to pursue and arrest the accomplices at large and bring them to justice. However, the day before yesterday, the suspect Gu suddenly falsely claimed that the hostage was hidden in Gu's residence at No. 12 Route des Sœurs in the French Concession. Detectives from the First District, together with detectives from the French police, went to search, but found no trace of the hostage. It is heard that the residence is the home of the first mastermind, Gu Zhong'an. However, Gu had already fled after hearing the news.

An Unheard-of Record of Six Mutes Involved in a Lawsuit 145

For a Debt of Five Hundred Yuan

Six Mutes Formed a Group to the Fifth District

Unable to Speak, They Used Writing Instead

Monetary Civil Cases Were Not Accepted

Lin Jiemu Was Also One of the Six Mutes

Hearing Lawsuits and Judging Cases Involves Labor and Pain; Aides Yell Orders - How Can it Be? However, the scene at the Fifth District Public Security Bureau yesterday morning, involving a mute lawsuit, seems to be an exception. Aside from the judge, there were a total of six mutes in the court. The interrogation and answers were conducted using writing instead of speech - this was truly strange. Even more coincidentally, the mute lover Lin Jiemu from the movies was also involved, appearing at the Public Security Bureau's preliminary hearing office at the same time as his five mute comrades. The mutes were suing over money matters because one of them was a "untrustworthy mute" who intended to evade the debt. Therefore, they argued and wrestled with each other until they reached the bureau seeking a judgment. However, the result was that "the matter concerns a civil case, and this district is not suitable to accept it. You should file a lawsuit in court." The six mutes quietly and silently, disappointedly went outside. As for whether they can maintain their original silent attitude in the future and avoid going to court, it is impossible to say. For now, let us record what happened yesterday morning as follows:

A Mute Borrowed Money, Mute People Guaranteed - Hu Tonggang, a mute, borrowed three hundred yuan from Mr. Su last spring on behalf of a friend. At that time, two copies of the IOU were drawn up, stipulating the interest, and guaranteed by Qin Jiping, Xu Jiansheng, Guo Mingli, and Yu Yuanqing, four fellow mutes. This was also meant to "prevent relying on verbal agreement, leaving this as proof." Later, Hu Tonggang also borrowed two hundred yuan from Mr. Su for his own wedding expenses, drawing up another IOU and, to avoid troubling others, again asked the four mutes to act as guarantors. Thus, although these four people did not utter a sound, the responsibility for the five hundred yuan debt had been lightly placed on each of their shoulders. The two IOUs quickly expired, but Hu and his friend had no money. The creditor had no choice but to urge the guarantors Qin, Xu, Guo, and Yu to pay. The four mutes then turned to Hu, pressing him to pay, but day after day, there was still no money. As the saying goes, "It is not the fierceness that is feared, but poverty." The four mutes were implicated due to the guarantee and had no way out. It was truly a case of a mute eating Coptis chinensis - suffering without being able to speak of it. Finally, yesterday morning around eleven o'clock, they had no choice but to drag Hu Tonggang to the Fifth District Public Security Bureau, accusing him of evading the debt. Guo, a member of the district, interrogated him.

A Mute Interrogation Using Writing - Aside from Qin, Xu, Guo, Yu, and the debtor Hu Tonggang, the five mutes, why was Lin Jiemu among them? Lin had no connection to this matter. However, because Lin is currently an assistant to lawyer Huang and has some connection and friendship with the mutes, he also participated, becoming part of the lawsuit of six mutes who went to the Fifth District Public Security Bureau as a group. The fact that mutes are involved in lawsuits is not unseen, but for a pure mute group like Lin and the others to go to the Public Security Bureau to file a complaint is unprecedented. At the time, the mutes gesticulated and acted, but the result was equal to zero. This is because the officers of the Public Security Bureau are used to investigating cases and making judgments, but seeing this group of people who want to speak but cannot do so, they can only sigh helplessly. Perhaps the teachers of schools for the deaf and mute would have some methods that could be used. Finally, Guo, a member of the district, gave each mute paper and pen, ordering each to write their background and the facts of the complaint. The mutes then spread out the paper and wielded the brush, expressing their hidden feelings on the paper.

Silent as Crows, Peaceful and Calm - The guarantors Qin Jiping, Xu Jiansheng, and Guo Mingli all work in the photography department of the Commercial Press on Baoshan Road. The debtor Hu Tonggang is also a colleague. Each time Guo, a member of the district, asked a question, he also used paper and pen as a medium. Everything that was said was replaced with writing. However, when the meaning was concise and the details were brief, they also nodded and raised their arms to indicate yes or no. Therefore, although there were more than ten people in the court, it was very quiet and silent as crows. According to what was written, Hu Tonggang spent a lot of money on his wedding on January 10 and is currently unable to repay the debt. Three hundred yuan of the debt was borrowed through an introduction, and two hundred yuan was for his own use. The four guarantors Qin and Xu referred to Hu as "untrustworthy" and "cunning," intending to evade the debt. Therefore, they twisted and controlled him. Guo, a member of the district, then devised a plan, ordering Hu to repay forty yuan per month, which would be cleared within a year. When the written note was shown to Hu, the mute frowned and furrowed his brow, shaking his head to indicate that he could not do so. Then he wrote that he was unable to repay. As a result, Guo, a member of the district, had to tell them that lawsuits involving money and debt are civil matters and that they could file a lawsuit in court, as the bureau could not handle it. After seeing the note, each mute slightly made a gesture of compliance, awkwardly left, and went out the door. According to what someone told the reporter, when these six people entered the door, they seemed to have a bellyful of words to say, and there was no lack of anger between their eyebrows. However, when questioned, they used writing instead of speech and remained silent, showing the best attitude. Therefore, this scene in court can also be called "peaceful and calm." If it were non-mutes, the shouting and noise would be indescribable.

Zhongxi Pharmacy Can Be Resolved Immediately

Other Stores Are Also Under Negotiation

Joint Shareholders Denied in Court

Plaintiff's Lawyer Presented Evidence

After the Shanghai Day and Night Bank and the Great World Amusement Savings Department went bankrupt, the French Concession Court held its sixth hearing yesterday. In the afternoon, Judge Gong presided over the court. First, accountant Pan Zhaobang stated that the Zhongxi Pharmacy part could be resolved in about two or three days. The remaining companies, such as Xuan Chang Company, the hot spring bathhouse, and the Great World, are currently under negotiation. As for those who owe money to each household and have not repaid, lawsuits have been filed. Many have already repaid, and twenty percent can be distributed in advance to each creditor, etc. Only four shareholders, Ye Shantao, Zhao Qinbo, Zhou Songqing, and Chen Xingwu, hired lawyers Lu Shaozong, Wang Weizhen, Wu Zhiping, etc. to defend, claiming that their clients were not shareholders of the joint company and asked what evidence the plaintiff had. Lawyer Yan Luqing stated that if the defendants were not shareholders, why did they not object when they were published in various newspapers? Now the Social Bureau has transferred the list of shareholders to Chen Tingrui and the other four lawyers for safekeeping. Today, they can ask Lawyer Chen to submit the case for detailed examination. Lawyer Chen Tingrui then presented the photographs of the shareholders' list to the court, stating that the salaries and travel expenses taken by each shareholder each month have handwritten seals as proof. The lawyer representing Ye Shantao and the others argued that this photograph could not be used as evidence and that the original and definitive evidence must be submitted to take effect. At this point, Lawyer Chen presented the original three volumes of the shareholders' list to the court for review. Accountant Pan requested that the court allow the shareholders' books to be transferred to the shareholders for review to convince them. Peng Qi, representing the Wanchun Silver Group, argued that the Wanchun Silver Group was organized by Yixing Qianzhuang and other households. Huang Chujiu went to Hangzhou for recuperation in December. Because the bank withdrew a lot of money, he returned to Shanghai and borrowed 300,000 yuan from the Wanchun Silver Group to repay each depositor. The method of paying the money was that the Day and Night Bank paid the depositors with promissory notes, which were transferred to each Qianzhuang for withdrawal. Each Qianzhuang then returned the notes to the Day and Night Bank, paying a total of 290,000 yuan. There is evidence that can be checked. Lawyer Yan Luqing then stood up and refuted that the Wanchun Silver Group contract was signed when Huang Chujiu was about to die, and the Day and Night Bank was in a panic of bankruptcy, which was invalid. The directors of the joint company cannot shirk their denial. Now the plaintiff has evidence to present, and each director should present counter-evidence. Lawyer Dong Yu stated that the money deposited by each creditor was hard-earned money and requested that the liquidator be instructed to distribute the money obtained first to provide relief. He also requested that the remaining part be disposed of as soon as possible to avoid consumption. Lawyer Tan Yigong, representing the Huang family, reported all of Huang Chujiu's property and detailed the real estate and movable property in a booklet to be submitted to the court for review. The lawyers then debated each other for a long time. Judge Gong approved the transfer of the three shareholders' lists submitted by Chen Tingrui and the other four lawyers and the evidence of the photographs submitted by the Wanchun Silver Group to accountants Pan and Wu for safekeeping.

The debate on the shareholders' part was postponed for fourteen days.

Spends Money and Gets Fooled

Is Detained Upon Arrival

A New Water Patrol Captain - At around eight o'clock yesterday morning, an uninvited guest suddenly arrived, well-dressed and carrying a letter of appointment in his hand (on which was written "Appointing Cheng Ding as Water Patrol Captain," etc., with complete seals). He went to the South City Water Patrol Headquarters to meet Captain Xu, claiming that he was named Cheng Ding and requesting a handover to take over the position. Captain Xu, believing that he had not received an order from his superiors to dismiss him, wondered where this unbelievable new captain came from. Therefore, he carefully examined the letter of appointment and discovered that it was forged. He immediately ordered the police to detain Cheng Ding, who claimed to be the new captain, for strict interrogation.

Spent One Hundred Silver Dollars - According to Cheng, he is twenty-four years old and from Nantong, Jiangsu. His brother is a rickshaw puller living at No. 4 London Road, Zhabei. I met a fellow villager named Cui Hao (Zi Lianen) at the Continental Hotel on Edward Road. We hit it off immediately. He claimed to be a good friend of the officials of the municipal authorities. Because I am currently unemployed, I mistakenly believed that he was a benefactor in front of me and could take the opportunity to promote me. I entrusted him to find me a position. He agreed readily and soon replied that the water patrol captain was about to be transferred, which was convenient to plot. However, I had to pay 400 yuan for the movement fee to get the letter of appointment to take office. I was overjoyed and returned home to first gather 100 silver dollars and give them to Cui. The remaining 300 yuan would be paid after I took office. Cui agreed and gave me the letter of appointment. Today, I came here hoping to take over the position smoothly. I didn't expect that the letter was forged and I was fooled. This is all Cui's fault alone, and I only lost one hundred yuan.

Plotting to Be the Third District Chief - He also said that there is one more thing I can tell you. Shen Changqing, who lives at No. 2, Lane 35, Huayuan Stone Bridge, Pudong, also asked Cui to plot to be the chief of the Third District of the Pudong Public Security Bureau at the Continental Hotel. I heard that he has succeeded and will take over soon. He is suffering the same fool as me.

Cui Still Lives in the Hotel - The captain checked the confession and immediately ordered detectives to go to the hotel, falsely claiming to visit Mr. Cui. The tea boy led them in to greet Cui. They also wanted to entrust Cui to find them a job. Cui replied that there was still a patrol officer vacancy in the water patrol team that he could plot. The detectives saw that Cui's tone had been recognized and showed the arrest warrant, taking Cui to the team. Cui suddenly changed his mind and refused to admit it. The captain ordered him to be interrogated more severely and sent to the Municipal Public Security Bureau for interrogation. He also notified Zhang, the chief of the Third District of Pudong, to go to the address to investigate Shen Changqing. Shen was not there, so he took his wife to the district for interrogation. His wife confessed that her husband had asked someone to plot to find a job outside, and she did not know anything about it. The district chief ordered her to stay in the district for further investigation.

Gu Yuncheng Seduce and Rape the Neighbor's Daughter 148

Because Gu Han Made an Alliance, He Was Involved in the Lawsuit

The Content Is Quite Related to Morality

The Trial Was Opened Yesterday, and the Public Was Prohibited from Attending

Gu Yuncheng, also known as Gu Peinai, is a young man in his twenties from Shanghai, residing at No. 108, Daqing Lane, Nanjing Road, originally from Haizhou, Jiangsu. Wu Xuemei, a woman from Changzhou, lives across the street at No. 101. Wu is two years older than Gu and has a beautiful appearance. She is a modern woman. Gu coveted her beauty and imitated the frivolous actions of Deng Tuzi. Every time the woman went out, he secretly followed her. However, the woman never succumbed to his seduction. Gu then changed his seduction techniques. Because his mother's bedroom was directly opposite the woman's embroidered room, he would often throw buttons at the woman's window. The woman worried that her parents would see it, so she rebuked Gu at the window for being rude. Gu did not feel humiliated but proud and sincerely apologized, expressing his admiration and saying that he wanted to make a connection with her. The woman then fell into his trick. Not only did she not avoid him as before, but she became increasingly close to him. They traveled together, and soon they made a white-headed alliance with each other. However, both parents were still unaware. One day, Gu asked the woman to go to the Hongkou Swimming Pool. On the way, they turned into a hotel and dreamed of Gaotang. Afterwards, they pretended to watch swimming to practice the agreement of Sang and Pu. It has been five years since then. The woman repeatedly asked Gu to ask her parents to formally hire someone to propose marriage, but Gu was always vague. The woman was already pregnant the year before and urged him even more urgently. Gu only replied that the time was not right and told the woman that if she was afraid of ruining her reputation, she could abandon the baby when it was born. Later, the woman's belly grew bigger and her parents knew. Because her face was at stake, she secretly gave the baby to others after giving birth and dared not publicize it. Gu then showed off his complacency and did not know how to avoid taboos. He openly went back and forth and combined until now. The money that the woman was defrauded of also reached over two thousand yuan. Recently, the woman felt that it was not a good outcome if it was not resolved for a long time, so she hired a lawyer to send a letter to Gu's parents, requesting that they get married as soon as possible. Gu's father, Quan Chang, then knew about it. He replied to the letter, agreeing that his son was an adult and that the parents would not restrict his marriage and would let him choose freely. The woman then urged Gu to hold the wedding, but Gu still used strict family education and the parents' disapproval as excuses. The woman realized that Gu had no intention of marrying her, but she had lost her chastity and lost her money, so she was unwilling and sued him for three crimes: harming morality, harming the family, and defrauding money to the Special District Court. The defendant was not present at the court hearing the other day, and the lawyer requested a postponement, saying that the defendant had gone to Qingdao and had not returned. Judge Cheng provisionally granted the request and postponed the hearing until yesterday afternoon. The defendant's lawyer said that the defendant had not returned to Shanghai. The plaintiff's lawyer asked the defendant to start the trial immediately because the defendant was intentionally evading. Judge Cheng then questioned the plaintiff about the process of falling in love. Because there were many details related to morality in this case, the court prohibited the public from attending. After questioning until dusk, the court adjourned and heard that a warrant would be issued to arrest the defendant Gu Yuncheng and investigate him.

Bandits Openly Extort 149

Repeatedly Invited to Hotels for Negotiations

Transfer Implemented on Xizang Road

Detectives Arrested by Surprise

Yan Songtao, the owner of the Xinjinji Construction Factory, had received six threatening letters in the past month, extorting money and agreeing to negotiate at a hotel on Zhejiang Road. Yan's residence is located at No. 317, Xin'er Lane, Datong Road, Xinzha. Therefore, according to intelligence, he requested the Xinzha Police Station to investigate. The police chief sent a detective to guard Room 214 of the hotel to observe the movements, but after guarding for a day, he did not see any traces of the bandits, thinking that the bandits had changed their plans. However, on Saturday evening of the previous week at dusk at 5:00 p.m., the postman delivered a letter to Yan's residence. After reading it, it was still a bandit letter, saying that even though you had implemented the previous agreement to clear the room at the hotel, there were too many people going there, so it was inconvenient to come out and negotiate. Now, I hereby renew the previous agreement and still use the hotel as the place for negotiation. You must go there on time. Yan reported the arrest again and sent detectives Ruan Yao and Yang Feizhang to the hotel to sit in a room. At about 3:00 p.m., the telephone in the room rang loudly. The detective held the microphone and heard the other party say: Are you Mr. Yan or Mr. Yan's representative? The detective reported as a representative. The other party continued to say: Is the payment ready? How much is it? Please tell me immediately. The detective replied: I have 200 or 300 gold. At this point, the bell rang again, and I did not hear what followed. An hour later, the bandit informed by phone to change the place of negotiation, asking to send someone with a calendar of the month, going west from the hotel to Xizang Road and turning north into Baike Road. Someone will be waiting on the way. Detective Yang followed the instructions, holding a calendar of the month in one hand and a paper bag in the other, pretending to be 300 yuan in the bag. He walked to Baike Road, and a person on the side of the road suddenly asked Yang if he was Mr. Yan's representative. Yang nodded and handed over the paper bag, returning to ask his name. This person took the bag and then wrote the two words Wang Kai and gave it to Yang. The detective expected that Wang Kai was the name of this bandit and unexpectedly grabbed him from behind and brought him back to the police station. The police chief interrogated him, and the bandit confessed that his name was Chen Yi from Hangzhou. The police chief asked who Wang Kai was and where he was hiding. He said that he was still waiting for him at the Sihai Shenping Lou teahouse on Fuzhou Road, waiting for him to return. When the detectives rushed to check and catch him, Wang had already checked out like Huang He. It turned out that they had a meeting time, and when they did not see him return after the time had passed, they knew that the incident had been revealed, so Wang escaped. Yesterday morning, the police station sent this bandit to the Special District Court. After Judge Ge Zhitian interrogated him, because the police station still had to investigate the accomplices to find out if there were any other cases, etc., which could not be determined at present, he ordered him to be temporarily detained pending investigation and further interrogation.

World Small Events 155

— Sea Guest

▲The transatlantic submarine telegraph began in 1858. The first telegram was from Queen Victoria of England, greeting the President of the United States.

▲The most valuable property of the natives of the African interior is cattle. They keep them permanently and never slaughter or sell them.

▲Someone in Folkestone, England, climbed to a 100-foot-high chimney and suddenly found a wren's nest with five young birds in it.

▲The music broadcast by wireless radio in Glasgow, Scotland, can also be heard by miners 330 feet below, 15 miles away. They use it as their only entertainment during working hours.

▲Bees in northern England had a great famine one year, said to be because the weather was particularly cold in the spring of that year, and hundreds of flowers bloomed late.

▲The Egyptian government presented two models of ancient water clocks to the Kensington Museum in England. One of them is the ancient clock from Karnak in Egypt, dating back to 1400 BC.

▲The world-famous Italian tenor Caruso earned no less than 500,000 pounds a year in royalties from recording records for major record companies during his lifetime.

Small Records of Huanghuagang and the Seventy-Two Martyrs' Tomb 156

— Li Qingduo

On March 29th of the Xinhai year, revolutionaries launched an uprising in Guangzhou to attack the Governor-General's Office of Guangdong and Guangxi. Seventy-two people died in the battle against the Qing officials, who were prepared. They were buried in Huanghuagang, known as the Huanghuagang Seventy-Two Martyrs' Tomb. Although the revolutionaries did not succeed in this battle, their iron-blooded souls served as pioneers of the revolution, chilling the Qing officials' hearts and souls. Their great achievements are enough to be immortalized. As we commemorate the seventy-two martyrs of Huanghuagang, please talk about the situation of Huanghuagang. Huanghuagang is located in the eastern suburbs of Guangzhou. It is necessary to pass through it on the way to Shahe Road. Enter through the tomb path first and go straight through the secluded path. Cars can directly reach the tomb. The entire tomb is built with stone and cement, and the shape is very magnificent. Ascend the steps for dozens of steps to reach the cemetery. The four sides of the cemetery are surrounded by stone railings, and flowers and trees are planted on both sides of the tomb, which is very elegant and clean. A stone memorial arch is built behind the tomb, with the memorial stones of the seventy-two martyrs donated by overseas party departments stacked on the upper end. The lower end has the words "Noble Spirit Will Last Forever" inscribed by President Sun, which are engraved on the stone wall. This was written in the tenth year of the Republic of China. The characters are grand and majestic. A music stage is built on the left side of the tomb, and a memorial monument to the seventy-two martyrs and a register of the seventy-two martyrs are built on the right side of the tomb, which are all browsed and read by visitors. There is also a memorial pavilion for tourists to rest. Every year on March 29th, the military and political leaders of Guangdong Province must lead all walks of life to pay tribute. The ceremony is very grand. The Shahe Road is very prosperous for a while. It is heard that many foreign tourist groups and foreign envoys who arrive in Guangdong also go to mourn, which shows that the loyalty and martyrdom of the seventy-two martyrs are deeply moving.

Effective Prescription for Treating Meningitis 157

— Jie Lu

Since the arrival of spring, meningitis has once again been rampant in various regions. Patients often die within a day or two, making it the most dreaded infectious disease of the season. In the spring of the year before last, this disease was prevalent in my hometown. My younger cousin's wife, Ms. Li, who had been married for less than half a year, suddenly contracted this epidemic. Initially, she felt headaches and sore throat, and soon after, she experienced vomiting, delirium, and a stiff neck. Chinese medicine was used to treat it as a spring epidemic, while Western medicine lacked available serum injection agents. Extracting fluid only caused the patient more suffering. Thus, this delicate and beautiful woman tragically passed away. Is it not a sorrowful event? In recent years, I have been frequently ill and lamenting the many unjust deaths in the world. I have studied medicine and suddenly realized that meningitis should be treated with cooling agents to achieve the most effective results. In the early stages, it is advisable to take Zijing Pills to detoxify and suppress vomiting, followed by medications such as Forsythia, Bai Ju Hua, Chrysanthemum, Kuding Tea, and Antelope Horn, which will surely bring about a miraculous recovery. As for preventive methods, one should use hair-removed and cleaned loquat leaves or white chrysanthemum to make tea for regular consumption. Gargling with salt water in the morning and tightly covering the mouth when going out are all essential preventive measures. This disease is more common in children, and it is most easily transmitted during the spring when the weather warms up. Therefore, children must be vaccinated and cautious about their diet and exposure to cold and heat. As for us adults, we should urgently pay attention to personal hygiene to strengthen our body's antitoxins, so that the fierce disease demon will surely retreat.

New Atmosphere in the Capital 158

— Hui Zi

▲ The Rapid Progress of Road Construction: The 7,500-meter-long Zhongshan Avenue has been praised by Chinese and foreign men and women as a top-tier tourist destination. Recently, the municipal government has been keenly focused on road construction. The most prosperous and bustling section of the Meridian Line Road, the Huapailou section, began construction yesterday. The street is being widened uniformly, with the storefronts on both sides being set back dozens of feet to create a wide avenue. The Commercial Press Branch and the Zhonghua Book Company, among others, are being demolished. The shacks and iron sheds along Zhongshan Road have been ordered by the police to be demolished within a limited time. Approximately 260 households north of the Drum Tower must relocate elsewhere immediately. From now on, those visiting the capital from various regions will no longer see only shacks and grass huts lining the streets upon entering the city, creating a desolate impression.

▲ The Rise and Fall of Entertainment Venues: Nanjing has nine movie theaters. The Guomin and Shijie theaters exclusively show sound films. The Xinguang and Zhongyang theaters show domestically produced films. The Mingxing, Shudu, and Datong theaters show silent films, while the Zhonghua theater has ceased operations in Nanjing, reportedly to install sound equipment. The Guomin theater is the most particular about its facilities, seating, location, and film selection, and therefore its business is the most prosperous. The Shijie and Nanjing theaters come next, but their business fluctuates. The Mingxing and Shudu theaters, both newly opened, are attracting customers by lowering prices, which shows the decline of the film industry. After all, the capital only has one-sixth of the total population of Shanghai, one-third of that of Beiping, and one-half of that of Tianjin. Where can one find so many customers? This is evidenced by the fact that the capital's two entertainment venues, the Dashijie and the Minye Company, are both suffering losses.

▲ The Establishment of the Military Medical Supervision Department: Since the Ministry of Health was reduced in scope to become the Health Administration, it could only accommodate 120 people. The positions of the remaining 100 to 200 people became a problem. Fortunately, the precedent of creating positions based on people's needs has been seen many times. Thus, the Military Medical Supervision Department was established. Because its functions overlap with those of the Military Medical Division of the Ministry of Military Affairs, they were divided so that the Military Medical Division handles military hygiene, while the Military Medical Supervision Department handles military medical education. It is nothing more than carving out a portion from within the scope of the Military Medical Division to establish a separate agency. The head of the Military Medical Supervision Department is a lieutenant general, and under him are more than 20 major general military doctors and more than 30 colonel military doctors, equivalent to a department under the Executive Yuan. A model military hospital is established separately, with the hospital director being a major general medical officer and the staff all being colonels. The organization of military hospitals in various units is much smaller than this. However, all military medical personnel are celebrating, saying, "We don't have to worry about not having a way out!"

Record of a Strange Habit: Sleeping on Gold 159

— Zui Chi Sheng

My neighbor is a Mrs. Zhang, who is over sixty years old. She is frugal and lives alone in a small room since her sons and daughters-in-law have moved out. She only employs a maid to serve her. She has been paralyzed and moaning in bed for a long time. Recently, she suddenly fell critically ill and passed away. When her family was preparing for the funeral, they examined her bed and found that her pillows and bedding were padded with silver dollars and banknotes almost everywhere, totaling several thousand silver dollars. It is said that the maid had been gradually pilfering some. These accumulated items were all savings from Mrs. Zhang's frugal living. However, since she did not store them in a bank or hide them in a chest, but used them as padding, it is quite amusing. Yesterday, I was drinking at a friend's house, and after a few drinks, I happened to mention this old woman's habit of sleeping on gold. Mr. Jiang, who was present, said, "This is nothing. I once had a landlord, Mr. Lu, who had been a comprador for a foreign firm. He was wealthy but extremely stingy. His wife and son had both passed away early, leaving only a personal maid. He died at the age of fifty, leaving behind a grandson who was only eight years old. The amount of gold he left hidden was quite shocking. When Mr. Lu was on his deathbed, he repeatedly pointed to his bedding, indicating something. His mattress was particularly thick, about five inches high. When it was opened, it was filled with HSBC banknotes, totaling 300,000 yuan. These two people share the same habit, but compared to Mr. Lu, the woman pales in comparison." I laughed and said, "Mr. Lu had wealth but could not use it, so he used 300,000 yuan as bedding, surrounding himself with money day and night, creating a new record in the history of misers. Even in death, Mr. Lu can be proud of himself. However, he treated money like his life, possessing huge sums of money without allowing it to circulate, and even depleting interest on it. Is this considered 'frugal' or 'extravagant'? I dare not comment. In short, his foolishness is unparalleled." Everyone said, "Then we drinkers are the ones who can thoroughly understand the 'philosophy of life.'" So we raised several large cups in succession.

Zui Chi Sheng also said: Our country, like the Northeast and Northwest regions, is full of resources everywhere. Yet, we hide gold in the ground without knowing how to develop it, instead inviting the covetousness of foreigners. The owners, in turn, worry about poverty every day and borrow foreign debts to support themselves. Compared to hiding gold in a bed, which can still be left to descendants, there seems to be a difference. So why should I criticize the woman and Mr. Lu?

Ten Thousand People Vie to See Zi Luolan 160

— Shuang Hong

Ms. Zi Luolan, a Cantonese singer and dancer, has come south again, and her reputation has grown even more. Ms. Zi Luolan is beautiful and talented with a naturally gifted voice.
